5:["$","p",null,{"children":"Figure 1: Proceeding video frames are generated from a world model given the context of the robot's task."}]
6:["$","h3",null,{"children":"Robotics Problem Statement"}]
7:["$","p",null,{"children":"Classical simulators such as Isaac Sim [1] and Mujoco [2] capture the physical dynamics necessary for training embodied agents, however the hardcoded dynamics used in such simulators is not practical for large-scale data generation of nuanced physical phenomena and realistic rendering.\nWorld models (also referred to as World Foundation Models or WFMs) offer an alternative, data-driven approach to simulation and future state prediction that can capture more nuanced physical phenomena and render realistic video/image outputs.\nWorld models are trained to capture the underlying spatial and temporal dynamics in images and video to predict future states of the environment.\nIn this document, we will look at four prevalent world models: GAIA-1 [3], Genie [4], TesserAct [5], and Cosmos [6]."}]
8:["$","h3",null,{"children":"Model Highlights"}]

17:["$","h2",null,{"children":"World Models for Robotics"}]
18:["$","h3",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Advantages"}]}]
19:["$","p",null,{"children":["World models act as the ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"digital twin of the world"}],", serving as a safe and efficient environment for simulating robot dynamics that can be used for:"]}]
1a:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Policy Evaluation and Initialization:"}]," WFMs can evaluate the quality of a policy model in a cost-effective virtual environment, allowing developers to rule out incapable policies before using physical resources.\nThey can also serve as a \"pre-trained\" initialization to address ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"data scarcity"}]," in real-world robotics."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Safe Policy Training:"}]," By pairing a WFM with a reward model, agents can gain proficiency through ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"reinforcement learning"}]," in a simulated environment that faithfully adheres to physical laws."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Planning and Model-Predictive Control (MPC):"}]," Robots can use world models to simulate multiple potential future states based on different action sequences, executing only the path that maximizes the predicted reward."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Synthetic Data Generation for Sim2Real:"}]," WFMs can generate massive amounts of synthetic video data, including metadata like ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"depth or semantic maps"}],", to bridge the gap between simulation and real-world deployment."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Imitation from Observation:"}]," Learned latent action spaces (as seen in Genie) allow agents to ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"imitate behaviors"}]," from action-free videos found on the Internet, potentially providing unlimited training data for generalist agents."]}],"\n"]}]
1b:["$","h3",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Limitations"}]}]
1c:["$","p",null,{"children":"WFMs have paved the way for practical robotics use-cases, but key limitations remain:"}]
1d:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Data and observability limits"}],": embodied, contact-rich interactions are underrepresented in large-scale datasets, and video-only observations cannot capture hidden state (e.g., forces, friction), limiting physics-faithful rollouts [11]."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Physical consistency failures"}],": long-horizon generations can violate object permanence and contact dynamics, making some models unreliable as safety-critical simulators [6]."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Weak closed-loop evidence"}],": GAIA-1 is a driving-focused generator rather than a deployable controller and is not evaluated in closed-loop autonomy [3].\nCosmos emphasizes scalable generation but lacks demonstrated closed-loop robotics performance [6].\nTesserAct reports downstream gains on manipulation benchmarks (e.g., RLBench) but remains compute-heavy and largely open-loop, leaving real-time/reactive control unresolved [5].\nGenie learns interactive latent actions from web video but is not validated as a robotics world model for contact-rich control [4]."]}],"\n"]}]

2a:["$","hr",null,{}]
2b:["$","h1",null,{"children":"Technical Paper Audit: GAIA-1"}]
2c:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Title"}],": GAIA-1: A Generative World Model for Autonomous Driving (Arxiv 2023)",["$","br",null,{}],"\n",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Authors"}],": Wayve",["$","br",null,{}],"\n",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Audit Authors"}],": Lorin Achey"]}]
2d:["$","hr",null,{}]
2e:["$","h2",null,{"children":"Summary"}]
2f:["$","p",null,{"children":"Autonomous driving requires the ability to predict future states of the world in order to plan safe actions, yet collecting real-world data for rare and dangerous scenarios is expensive, risky, and often impossible.\nGAIA-1 introduces a generative world model for autonomous driving that combines autoregressive sequence modeling with video diffusion decoding to generate controllable driving scenarios.\nThe model accepts video, text, and action inputs, encoding them into discrete tokens and predicting future states autoregressively.\nGAIA-1 demonstrates the ability to generate coherent scenes with realistic object interactions that were not explicitly provided in the training data.\nHowever, the model does not run in real-time and lacks closed-loop evaluation, making its utility for actual autonomous driving control questionable."}]
30:["$","hr",null,{}]
31:["$","h2",null,{"children":"1. Problem Domain & Taxonomy"}]
32:["$","h3",null,{"children":"1.1 The Technical Challenge"}]
33:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Core Problem"}],": GAIA-1 addresses the challenge of building generative world models for autonomous driving that can predict future states of the environment while being controllable through both high-level commands (text) and low-level control signals (speed/curvature)."]}]
34:["$","p",null,{"children":"Autonomous driving requires a model that can imagine futures given a proposed action, generate synthetic training data for rare and dangerous scenarios that cannot be safely collected in the real world, and enable planning by evaluating multiple action sequences before committing to one.\nThe authors claim that neither traditional world models (which capture dynamics but lack visual fidelity) nor generative video models (which achieve realism but lack dynamics understanding) can solve this problem alone."}]
1a9:T4e4, Prior world models such as MuZero [9], Dreamer [13], and MILE [11] have demonstrated success in simulated environments but struggle to capture the full complexity of real-world driving.
These approaches typically rely on labeled data (e.g. segmentation masks, depth maps, 3D bounding boxes) which is expensive to obtain and difficult to scale to the millions of hours needed for robust autonomous driving.
Furthermore, models trained primarily on synthetic data suffer from a simulation-to-real gap, where the policies they learn fail when deployed on actual vehicles encountering real-world nuances like unusual lighting, weather, or road conditions.
Perhaps most critically, these models compress visual scenes into low-dimensional latent representations (typically 256-512 dimensions), which cannot faithfully reconstruct fine details such as distant pedestrians or subtle road textures.
VAE-based approaches in particular tend to produce blurry outputs due to optimizing a lower bound on the likelihood rather than the true distribution.
For example, Dreamer-v3 achieves superhuman performance on Atari games but operates on 64×64 grayscale images which is far below the 1920×1080 RGB video resolution required for real-world driving perception.35:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Traditional World Models and Realism."}],"$1a9"]}]
36:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Generative Video Models and Dynamics Understanding."}]," Modern video generation systems like Imagen Video [16] and Make-A-Video [68] can produce photorealistic content, yet they fundamentally lack the world understanding necessary for autonomous driving.\nThey can generate plausible-looking frames without modeling the causal structure of the world, potentially producing physics-violating scenarios where objects teleport or pass through each other.\nGeneration is largely uncontrollable: one cannot easily specify \"add a pedestrian crossing the street\" or \"change the weather to rain\" to synthesize targeted training scenarios for edge cases.\nMost fundamentally, these models treat video as a sequence of images rather than as the evolution of a world state, lacking the ability to reason about object permanence, velocities, and interactions over time.\nImagen Video can generate a compelling video of \"a car driving through Tokyo,\" but it cannot answer the safety-critical question \"what happens if that car brakes suddenly?\""]}]
37:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"GAIA-1's Proposed Solution."}]," GAIA-1 addresses this dual challenge by using two specialized components: a world model that reasons about high-level scene components and dynamics (answering \"what happens next?\"), and a video diffusion decoder that translates these latent predictions into high-quality pixel-space video (answering \"what does it look like?\").\nThis architectural separation allows each component to benefit from its respective scaling paradigm."]}]
38:["$","h3",null,{"children":"1.2 Taxonomy of Approaches & Related Work"}]
39:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Classical Planning Methods."}]," Early autonomous driving systems relied on rule-based approaches where engineers attempted to manually specify the complete set of driving behaviors.\nThese systems encode expert knowledge as explicit if-then rules - for example, \"if a pedestrian is detected within 10 meters, apply brakes.\"\nWhile interpretable, such approaches are fundamentally brittle: the complexity of real-world driving makes it impossible to anticipate every scenario in advance.\nModel Predictive Control (MPC) offered a more principled alternative by optimizing trajectories over a finite horizon using hand-crafted cost functions and dynamics models.\nHowever, MPC requires accurate models of vehicle dynamics and the environment, struggles with the computational demands of real-time replanning, and cannot easily incorporate learned priors about human behavior or scene semantics."]}]
3a:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Imitation Learning."}]," The advent of deep learning enabled a shift toward learning driving policies directly from human demonstrations.\nKendall et al. [1] demonstrated that an end-to-end neural network could learn to drive in a day by imitating expert behavior.\nHowever, imitation learning suffers from distribution shift: the policy encounters states during deployment that differ from the training distribution, leading to compounding errors.\nAdditionally, imitation learning cannot imagine scenarios beyond those present in the training data.\nIt learns to mimic expert actions but not to reason about predicted futures or recover from novel situations."]}]
3b:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"World Models."}]," To address the limitations of pure imitation, researchers developed world models that learn to predict future states of the environment.\nHa and Schmidhuber [7] introduced recurrent world models that enabled policy learning entirely within a learned \"dream\" environment.\nMuZero [9] demonstrated that planning with a learned model could achieve superhuman performance in games like Go, Chess, and Atari without access to ground-truth game rules.\nFor autonomous driving specifically, MILE [11] combined model-based prediction with imitation learning for urban driving, while DayDreamer [15] showed that world models could enable sample-efficient learning on physical robots.\nDreamer-v3 [13] unified these ideas into a general framework capable of mastering diverse domains through latent imagination.\nHowever, as discussed above, these approaches typically operate in low-dimensional latent spaces that sacrifice visual fidelity."]}]
3c:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Video Generation and World Models."}]," The most recent evolution casts world modeling as a video generation problem.\nThis approach builds on two parallel developments: sequence modeling formulations that treat control as token prediction (Decision Transformer [19], Trajectory Transformer [10]), and large-scale video generation systems that produce photorealistic content (Imagen Video [16], Make-A-Video [68]).\nGAIA-1 synthesizes these paradigms, using autoregressive sequence modeling for world dynamics and diffusion models for high-fidelity rendering.\nConcurrent work includes DriveGAN [62], which uses GANs for controllable driving simulation, and DriveDreamer [87],\nwhich applies diffusion models conditioned on 3D scene layouts."]}]
3d:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Comparative Positioning."}],"\nGAIA-1 distinguishes itself from related work through scale (9.4B parameters vs. ~100M-1B for competitors),\ngeneration quality (video diffusion vs. VAE/GAN), and multimodal conditioning (text + action).\nHowever, it sacrifices real-time capability (unlike MILE, DriveGAN, Dreamer-v3) and closed-loop evaluation (unlike MILE, Dreamer-v3).\nMILE provides trajectory outputs evaluated on CARLA driving; GAIA-1 provides video outputs with qualitative evaluation only."]}]

3f:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Evolution of Problem Formulation (2021-2023)"}],":"]}]
40:["$","ol",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Representation Shift"}],": From pixel-level prediction to discrete token prediction"]}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Enables scaling laws similar to LLMs"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"GAIA-1 uses VQ-VAE [28] with DINO [30] distillation for semantic tokenization"}],"\n"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Control Paradigm Shift"}],": From end-to-end driving to controllable generation"]}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"GAIA-1 separates \"understanding the world\" from \"controlling the vehicle\""}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Enables synthetic data generation for downstream policy training"}],"\n"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Evaluation Shift"}],": From closed-loop performance to open-loop video quality"]}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Scene Quality vs. Driving Quality"}],": GAIA-1 provides only qualitative evaluation, largely focused on scene generation"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"No downstream driving policy is trained so it is unclear whether an autonomous system can drive better after being trained on GAIA-1 synthetic data"}],"\n"]}],"\n"]}],"\n"]}]

42:["$","h2",null,{"children":"2. Architectural Overview"}]
43:["$","h3",null,{"children":"2.1 Model Architecture"}]
44:["$","p",null,{"children":"GAIA-1 adopts a three-stage pipeline that separates perception (tokenization), reasoning (world model), and rendering (video decoder).\nThis factorization allows each component to be optimized independently and benefit from domain-specific scaling paradigms: the tokenizer compresses visual information into a discrete vocabulary, the world model applies LLM-style autoregressive prediction over this vocabulary, and the video decoder uses diffusion to render high-fidelity output."}]
45:["$","table",null,{"children":[["$","thead",null,{"children":["$","tr",null,{"children":[["$","th",null,{"children":"Component"}],["$","th",null,{"children":"Parameters"}],["$","th",null,{"children":"Function"}]]}]}],["$","tbody",null,{"children":[["$","tr",null,{"children":[["$","td",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Image Tokenizer"}]}],["$","td",null,{"children":"0.3B"}],["$","td",null,{"children":"Discrete image encoding (VQ-VAE [28] + DINO [30])"}]]}],["$","tr",null,{"children":[["$","td",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"World Model"}]}],["$","td",null,{"children":"6.5B"}],["$","td",null,{"children":"Autoregressive next-token prediction"}]]}],["$","tr",null,{"children":[["$","td",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Video Decoder"}]}],["$","td",null,{"children":"2.6B"}],["$","td",null,{"children":"Diffusion-based video rendering"}]]}]]}]]}]
46:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","img",null,{"src":"./figures-system-diagrams-images/Figure2-SystemDiagram-GAIA1.png","alt":"GAIA-1 Architecture"}]}]
47:["$","p",null,{"children":"The data flow proceeds as follows: (1) Input video frames are encoded into discrete image tokens via the tokenizer; (2) Text descriptions are embedded via frozen T5-Large [24]; (3) Actions (speed, curvature) are projected via learned linear layers; (4) All modalities are interleaved into a single sequence and processed by the autoregressive world model to predict future image tokens; (5) Predicted tokens are decoded into video frames via the diffusion decoder."}]

6d:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Autoregressive vs. Parallel Decoding."}]," The world model generates tokens sequentially rather than in parallel (like MaskGIT or BERT [90]).\nThis maximizes expressiveness - each token can depend on all previous tokens - but incurs 576 sequential forward passes per frame.\nA parallel decoder could achieve ~36× speedup but would sacrifice the ability to model complex inter-token dependencies.\nGAIA-1 prioritizes quality over inference speed, a choice aligned with research exploration rather than deployment."]}]
6e:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Temporal Resolution (6.25 Hz vs. 25 Hz)."}]," The world model operates at 6.25 Hz (160ms between frames) to keep sequence length tractable, with the video decoder upsampling to 25 Hz.\nThis reduces attention memory by ~15× compared to native 25 Hz, enabling 4-second context windows.\nHowever, 160ms between predictions means a vehicle at highway speed moves 4.8m between frames - fine-grained motion and sudden events may be aliased away before the model sees them."]}]

85:["$","h3",null,{"children":"4.3 Engineering Bottlenecks"}]
86:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Information Decay."}]," The tokenizer compresses 3.5M bits to 7,488 bits (470×).\nSub-pixel depth gradients, high-frequency textures, precise object boundaries, and small/distant objects may fall below tokenization resolution."]}]
87:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"The Semantic-Motor Gap."}]," GAIA-1 outputs video frames, not control commands.\nA complete system requires an additional perception-to-control policy that processes generated video, extracts state, plans trajectory, and outputs motor commands.\nAs the authors state, GAIA-1 is intended as \"a valuable neural simulator\" for data generation - it is a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"data augmentation tool"}],", not a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"driving policy"}],"."]}]
88:["$","hr",null,{}]
89:["$","h2",null,{"children":"5. Critical Synthesis & Sign-Off"}]
8a:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.1 Load-Bearing Assumptions"}]
8b:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Assumption 1: Discrete Tokenization Preserves Driving-Critical Information."}]," The 576 tokens with K=8192 vocabulary are claimed to sufficiently represent driving scenes, but DINO distillation biases toward semantic categories over geometric precision, and 16× downsampling destroys sub-16-pixel details.\nA pedestrian 50m away may occupy <16 pixels and be compressed away entirely."]}]
8c:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Assumption 2: Next-Token Prediction = World Understanding."}]," The paper claims emergent \"understanding of geometry\" and \"scene dynamics,\" but provides no quantitative validation.\nPerceptual realism does not equal physical accuracy; the model may memorize dataset patterns rather than learn causal dynamics."]}]
8d:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Assumption 3: Proprietary UK Data Generalizes."}]," 4,700 hours of London driving (right-hand traffic, urban, UK climate) cannot cover left-hand-drive countries, highways, rural areas, or diverse driving cultures."]}]
8e:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Assumption 4: Generation Quality to Policy Performance."}]," No evidence that GAIA-1 generations improve downstream driving.\nDomain gap and generation artifacts may harm transfer."]}]
8f:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.2 Reproducibility Assessment"}]
90:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Code publicly available? ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"No"}]]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Pre-trained models released? ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"No"}]]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Dataset accessible? ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"No"}]," (proprietary)"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Hyperparameters specified? ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Yes"}]]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Quantitative evaluation? ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"No"}]]}],"\n"]}]
91:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Score: 1/5 - Not reproducible."}]}]
92:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.3 Failure Modes"}]
93:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Transparent/Reflective Objects"}],": Tokenizer has no explicit transparency representation; generated videos may show objects appearing/disappearing through glass or inconsistent reflections."]}]
94:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"High-Velocity Objects"}],": At 6.25 Hz, objects moving at 27 m/s cover 4.3m between frames; sudden appearances cannot be predicted."]}]
95:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Multi-Vehicle Coordination"}],": Model generates plausible individual behaviors but may violate coordination rules at ambiguous intersections."]}]
96:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Weather Transitions"}],": Text conditioning sets static weather; transitions (tunnel entry, sudden rain) may be abrupt or inconsistent."]}]
97:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.4 The Next 10,000 GPU-Hour Experiment"}]
98:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Proposed"}],": Closed-loop evaluation.\nGenerate 1,000 hours of diverse scenarios with GAIA-1, train downstream policy on generated data, evaluate in CARLA/nuScenes [2] (collision rate, route completion, comfort metrics), compare to real-data-only baseline.\nThis would quantify the actual utility of world model generations for policy training."]}]
99:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.5 Foundational vs. Incremental"}]
9a:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Foundational"}],": First large-scale (9.4B) multimodal world model for real driving; demonstrates LLM scaling laws transfer; shows emergent properties (multi-agent reasoning, 3D geometry, extrapolation); architectural template likely influential."]}]
9b:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Incremental"}],": No quantitative evaluation or reproducible benchmarks; cannot run in real-time by orders of magnitude; proprietary and not reproducible; no demonstration of downstream utility."]}]
9c:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Verdict"}],": GAIA-1 is ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"foundational as a research direction"}]," but ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"incremental as a deployable system"}],".\nIt proves world models can scale but doesn't solve the grounding problem."]}]
9d:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.6 Sign-Off"}]

ba:["$","h1",null,{"children":"Technical Paper Audit: TesserAct"}]
bb:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Title"}],": TesserAct: Learning 4D Embodied World Models (arxiv 2025)",["$","br",null,{}],"\n",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Authors"}],": Haoyu Zhen et al.",["$","br",null,{}],"\n",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Audit Authors"}],": Lorin Achey"]}]
bc:["$","hr",null,{}]
bd:["$","h2",null,{"children":"Summary"}]
be:["$","p",null,{"children":"Embodied agents require world models that capture the 3D structure of scenes to enable precise manipulation, yet existing world models operate in 2D pixel space, losing critical depth and pose information.\nTesserAct addresses this by learning a 4D embodied world model that predicts RGB-DN (RGB, Depth, Normal) videos, providing a compact yet geometrically rich representation of scene dynamics.\nThe model fine-tunes CogVideoX on a curated dataset of ~285k robotic manipulation videos annotated with depth and normal maps, then reconstructs temporally and spatially consistent 4D point clouds via normal integration with novel consistency losses.\nTesserAct enables downstream action planning through an inverse dynamics model, outperforming 2D video-based approaches on RLBench manipulation tasks.\nHowever, the single-view RGB-DN representation captures only visible surfaces, and the approach inherits the inference cost limitations of video diffusion models."}]
bf:["$","hr",null,{}]
c0:["$","h2",null,{"children":"1. Problem Domain & Taxonomy"}]
c1:["$","h3",null,{"children":"1.1 The Technical Challenge"}]
c2:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Core Problem"}],": TesserAct addresses the fundamental limitation that existing world models operate in 2D pixel space, which fails to capture the 3D spatial relationships essential for robotic manipulation.\nWithout accurate depth and 6-DoF pose estimations, robotic systems struggle to determine the exact position and orientation of objects."]}]
c3:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"The 2D Representation Gap."}]," Prior video-based world models like UniPi [15], Genie [8], and Pandora [64] generate future video frames conditioned on actions and text, but their 2D outputs suffer from several critical limitations for embodied tasks.\nFirst, they cannot provide metric depth information needed to plan precise grasping motions - a robot arm must know not just where an object appears in the image but how far it is and at what angle.\nSecond, 2D models can produce geometrically inconsistent outputs where object sizes and shapes vary across frames, violating physical constraints.\nThird, converting 2D predictions back to 3D control signals requires additional perception modules (depth estimators, pose estimators) that introduce error accumulation and latency.\nThe paper notes that \"without accurate depth and 6-DoF pose estimations, robotic systems struggle to determine the exact position and orientation of objects.\""]}]
c4:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"The 4D Training Data Gap."}]," While 3D and 4D representations would better serve robotics, collecting large-scale datasets with ground-truth depth and normal maps is prohibitively expensive.\nReal-world depth sensors (LiDAR, structured light) have limited resolution and fail on reflective/transparent surfaces common in manipulation scenarios.\nSynthetic data provides perfect ground truth but suffers from sim-to-real gaps.\nThis data scarcity has prevented prior work from training 4D world models at scale."]}]
c5:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"TesserAct's Proposed Solution."}]," TesserAct addresses these challenges through three key innovations: (1) an RGB-DN representation that jointly predicts RGB, depth, and normal maps as a lightweight proxy for full 4D scenes; (2) a data annotation pipeline using off-the-shelf depth/normal estimators to augment existing robotic video datasets; and (3) a 4D reconstruction algorithm with novel consistency losses to convert RGB-DN videos into temporally coherent point clouds.\nThis factorization leverages existing video diffusion priors while adding geometric structure needed for robotics."]}]
c6:["$","h3",null,{"children":"1.2 Taxonomy of Approaches & Related Work"}]
c7:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Embodied Foundation Models."}]," Recent work has focused on constructing foundation models for general-purpose agents through two main approaches.\nVision-Language-Action (VLA) models like RT-2 [6] and OpenVLA [34] directly output action tokens from image and text inputs, learning an end-to-end mapping from perception to control.\nMultimodal language models like PaLM-E [13] output text describing actions.\nBoth approaches aim to construct foundation model policies but do not model world dynamics explicitly.\nIn contrast, TesserAct constructs a foundation world model that can be used for downstream planning and policy synthesis."]}]
c8:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"World Models for Control."}]," Learning dynamics models given control inputs has been studied extensively in model-based reinforcement learning and optimal control.\nEarly approaches like Dreamer [22] learned world models in low-dimensional latent spaces, which are efficient but difficult to generalize across environments.\nHa and Schmidhuber's [21] recurrent world models enabled policy learning in \"dream\" environments but operated on simple games.\nMore recent work like UniPi [15] and Pandora [64] uses video diffusion models as world models, but these operate over 2D pixels.\nTesserAct extends this paradigm to 4D by jointly predicting depth and normal information."]}]
c9:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"4D Video Generation."}]," The task of generating dynamic 3D content has gained attention through approaches combining diffusion models with NeRF [44] or Gaussian splatting [33].\nHowever, these methods suffer from slow optimization due to hybrid frameworks and SDS loss convergence challenges.\nTesserAct sidesteps these issues by representing 4D scenes as RGB-DN videos, which are more efficient to generate and provide high-accuracy 3D information.\nThe paper notes that \"our approach is the first to directly predict 4D scenes from the current frame and the embodied agent's action described in text.\""]}]
ca:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Comparative Positioning."}]," TesserAct distinguishes itself from related work by: (1) providing explicit 3D geometry (depth, normal) rather than implicit 2D features; (2) enabling temporally consistent 4D reconstruction rather than frame-by-frame estimation; (3) demonstrating downstream utility for robotic manipulation rather than just generation quality.\nCompared to 3D-VLA [76] which predicts only goal states, TesserAct models the full trajectory.\nCompared to Aether [57] which trains on synthetic data without language grounding, TesserAct supports language-conditioned control on real data."]}]
cb:["$","h3",null,{"children":"1.3 The \"Initial Dissolve\""}]
cc:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Evolution of Problem Formulation (2023-2025)"}],":"]}]
cd:["$","ol",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"From 2D to 4D World Models"}],": Prior video world models treated scenes as sequences of images; TesserAct treats them as evolving 3D geometry."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"From Implicit to Explicit Geometry"}],": Rather than hoping 2D representations implicitly capture 3D structure, TesserAct explicitly predicts depth and normal maps that can be directly used for 3D reconstruction."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"From Generation to Reconstruction"}],": TesserAct's value proposition is not just generating plausible videos but reconstructing geometrically accurate 4D scenes that enable downstream robotic control."]}],"\n"]}],"\n"]}]
ce:["$","hr",null,{}]
cf:["$","h2",null,{"children":"2. Architectural Overview"}]
d0:["$","h3",null,{"children":"2.1 Model Architecture"}]
d1:["$","p",null,{"children":"TesserAct extends CogVideoX [69], a latent video diffusion model, to jointly predict RGB, depth, and normal videos.\nThe architecture preserves the pretrained video generation capability while adding geometric prediction heads."}]
d2:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","img",null,{"src":"./figures-system-diagrams-images/Architecture-Fig2-TesserAct.png","alt":"TesserAct Architecture"}]}]
d3:["$","p",null,{"children":"The data flow proceeds as follows: (1) RGB, depth, and normal videos are separately encoded by the frozen CogVideoX 3D VAE; (2) Three separate input projectors extract embeddings for each modality; (3) The DiT backbone processes the sum of embeddings conditioned on text instruction and diffusion timestep; (4) RGB output uses the original CogVideoX projector; (5) Depth and normal outputs use additional Conv3D + MLP projectors that combine hidden states with RGB predictions."}]
d4:["$","h3",null,{"children":"2.2 RGB-DN Video Prediction"}]
d5:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Core Innovation"}],": Rather than predicting explicit 3D representations (meshes, point clouds, NeRFs [44]), TesserAct predicts RGB-DN (RGB, Depth, Normal) videos as a compact 4D proxy."]}]
d6:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Why RGB-DN?"}]," This representation offers three advantages:"]}]
d7:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Computational efficiency"}],": Same dimensionality as standard video, enabling use of pretrained video models"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Geometric completeness"}],": Depth provides metric distance; normals provide surface orientation - together sufficient for 3D reconstruction"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Temporal modeling"}],": Video diffusion naturally captures dynamics, unlike per-frame 3D estimation"]}],"\n"]}]

fe:["$","h3",null,{"children":"2.5 Key Architectural Trade-Offs"}]
ff:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Joint vs. Separate Modality Prediction."}]," TesserAct predicts RGB, depth, and normal jointly through a shared backbone rather than using separate models for each.\nThis enables cross-modal reasoning - depth predictions can leverage RGB texture cues, normals can condition on depth edges - but creates a more complex training objective.\nThe alternative (separate estimators applied post-hoc) would lose temporal consistency and cross-modal coherence."]}]
100:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Pretrained Video Model vs. Training from Scratch."}]," With only ~285k training videos (far less than the billions used for CogVideoX), training from scratch is infeasible.\nFine-tuning preserves video generation priors while adding geometric capability.\nThe trade-off is inheriting CogVideoX's biases and architecture constraints."]}]
101:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"RGB-DN vs. Full 3D Representation."}]," Point clouds, meshes, or NeRFs would provide more complete 3D information, but are computationally expensive to generate and lack mature pretrained models.\nRGB-DN is a middle ground: richer than 2D pixels, cheaper than full 3D, and compatible with video diffusion architectures."]}]

114:["$","h3",null,{"children":"4.1 Downstream Action Planning"}]

117:["$","ol",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Reconstruct 4D point clouds from RGB-DN predictions"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Filter background/floor, sample 8192 points"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Encode point cloud via PointNet [49]"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Concatenate with instruction language embedding"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"4-layer MLP outputs 7-DoF actions"}],"\n"]}]

11a:["$","p",null,{"children":"TesserAct outperforms 2D baselines on 7/9 tasks, with largest gains on tasks requiring geometric understanding (close box, open drawer, open jar)."}]
11b:["$","h3",null,{"children":"4.2 The Precision Gap"}]
11c:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Where 4D Helps"}],": Tasks requiring precise spatial reasoning benefit from explicit geometry:"]}]
11d:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Grasping"}],": Point cloud provides 3D object pose for grasp planning"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Tool use"}],": Sweep dustpan, water plants require understanding tool-object relationships"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Contact-rich tasks"}],": Close box, open jar need accurate surface geometry"]}],"\n"]}]
11e:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Where 4D Doesn't Help"}],": Open microwave and weighing off show comparable or worse performance than UniPi*.\nThe paper suggests \"these tasks already have sufficient information in the 2D front image.\"\nThis reveals that 4D is not universally beneficial - some tasks are solvable from 2D cues."]}]
11f:["$","h3",null,{"children":"4.3 Engineering Bottlenecks"}]
120:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Single-Surface Limitation"}],": RGB-DN from a single viewpoint captures only visible surfaces.\nThe paper acknowledges: \"our RGB-DN representation of a 4D world model is cheap and easy to predict, it only captures a single surface of the world.\"\nFor manipulation requiring reasoning about occluded regions or object backsides, this is insufficient."]}]
121:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Depth Estimation Quality on Real Data"}],": Real-world depth annotations come from RollingDepth [31] (affine-invariant, not metric).\nConverting to metric depth for control requires scale disambiguation, which may introduce errors.\nThe paper doesn't report metric depth accuracy on real data."]}]
122:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Inference Latency"}],": Video diffusion models are slow.\nTesserAct requires 50 DDPM sampling steps for 49-frame generation.\nThe paper reports novel view synthesis in \"~1 min\" vs Shape of Motion's [62] \"~2 hours.\"\nIt does not report end-to-end latency for closed-loop control.\nReal-time operation (10+ Hz) is likely infeasible."]}]
123:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Action Space Mismatch"}],": The inverse dynamics model predicts 7-DoF actions from point clouds, but this requires knowing keyframes a priori.\nThe paper notes they \"predict and record all future keyframes\" then \"query the inverse dynamic model\" - this open-loop execution precludes reactive control."]}]
124:["$","hr",null,{}]
125:["$","h2",null,{"children":"5. Critical Synthesis & Sign-Off"}]
126:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.1 Load-Bearing Assumptions"}]
127:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Assumption 1: RGB-DN is Sufficient for 4D Understanding."}],"\nThe paper assumes that RGB, depth, and normal maps from a single viewpoint provide enough geometric information for manipulation.\nThis assumption may fail for occluded geometry and tasks that require multi-view reasoning.\nThe ~10% of tasks where TesserAct underperforms may reveal these limits."]}]
128:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Assumption 2: Estimated Depth/Normal is Accurate Enough."}]," Real-world training uses RollingDepth and Marigold estimates, not ground truth.\nSystematic estimation errors will be learned by the model.\nNo analysis of how estimation quality affects downstream performance is provided."]}]
129:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Assumption 3: Cross-Embodiment Transfer Works."}]," Training on 4 robot types is claimed to enable generalization, but all evaluation is on seen embodiments (Franka Panda on RLBench).\nTrue cross-embodiment generalization to novel robots is unvalidated."]}]
12a:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Assumption 4: Video Diffusion Priors Transfer to Robotics."}]," CogVideoX was trained on web videos, not robotic manipulation.\nThe assumption that its priors (object permanence, physics, motion) transfer to embodied scenarios is implicit but unverified."]}]
12b:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.2 Reproducibility Assessment"}]
12c:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Code publicly available? ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Yes"}]," (website linked)"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Pre-trained models released? ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Unclear"}]]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Dataset accessible? ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Partially"}]," (annotations on public datasets)"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Hyperparameters specified? ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Yes"}]]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Quantitative evaluation? ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Yes"}]," (FVD, depth metrics, success rates)"]}],"\n"]}]
12d:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Score: 3/5 - Partially reproducible."}],"\nThe use of public datasets with annotation pipeline and provided metrics enables validation, though model weights and some implementation details may be missing."]}]
12e:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.3 Failure Modes"}]
12f:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Occlusion Failures"}],": Single-view RGB-DN cannot reason about occluded geometry.\nTasks requiring reaching behind objects or reasoning about hidden surfaces will fail."]}]
130:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Dynamic Scene Failures"}],": The optical flow-based consistency assumes distinguishable static/dynamic regions.\nFast motions, motion blur, or scenes with large dynamic regions may break the reconstruction."]}]
131:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Out-of-Distribution Embodiments"}],": Despite claiming cross-embodiment capability, no evaluation on truly novel robot morphologies is provided.\nA hexapod or humanoid would likely fail."]}]
132:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Transparent/Reflective Objects"}],": Like most depth estimators, RollingDepth and Marigold struggle with non-Lambertian surfaces.\nGenerated depth/normal for glass, mirrors, or metallic objects may be unreliable."]}]
133:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.4 The Next 10,000 GPU-Hour Experiment"}]
134:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Proposed"}],": Multi-view RGB-DN generation.\nTrain a model to predict RGB-DN from multiple viewpoints simultaneously, enabling full 3D reconstruction rather than single-surface capture.\nThis directly addresses the paper's stated limitation and would enable reasoning about occluded regions."]}]
135:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Alternative"}],": Real-time distillation.\nDistill TesserAct into a smaller model capable of 10+ Hz inference for closed-loop control, then evaluate reactive manipulation performance."]}]
136:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.5 Foundational vs. Incremental"}]
137:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Foundational"}],": First demonstration that video diffusion models can be extended to 4D embodied world modeling with explicit geometry; RGB-DN representation as efficient 4D proxy; novel consistency losses for temporal coherence; demonstrated downstream utility for manipulation."]}]
138:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Incremental"}],": Single-view limitation restricts true 4D understanding; inherits video diffusion inference costs; evaluation limited to seen embodiments and relatively simple tasks; no scaling analysis."]}]
139:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Verdict"}],": TesserAct is ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"foundational for the RGB-DN representation and reconstruction pipeline"}]," but ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"incremental for embodied AI capability"}],".\nIt proves that adding geometry to video world models helps robotics, but the single-view limitation and inference cost prevent deployment."]}]
13a:["$","h3",null,{"children":"5.6 Sign-Off"}]
13b:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"If this paper were a technical proposal at a robotics company, would I sign off?"}]}]
13c:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"For Production: CONDITIONAL NO"}]}]

15b:["$","h1",null,{"children":"Technical Paper Audit: Cosmos"}]
15c:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Title"}],": Cosmos: World Foundation Model Platform for Physical AI (arXiv 2025)\n",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Authors"}],": NVIDIA\n",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Audit Author"}],": Carson Kohlbrenner"]}]
15d:["$","hr",null,{}]
15e:["$","h2",null,{"children":"1. Summary"}]
15f:["$","p",null,{"children":"Cosmos is NVIDIA's proposed generalized solution for the lack of data available for physical systems that interact with the world.\nCosmos is a generalized world foundation model that can be fine-tuned for specific use cases such as robotics, autonomous driving, and synthetic data generation by predicting future states of the systems.\nCosmos uses a mixture of discrete and continuous latent representations to support transformer-based diffusion models and transformer-based autoregressive models, which each have trade-offs regarding the visual fidelity of predictions and symbolic reasoning."}]
160:["$","hr",null,{}]

16a:["$","p",null,{"children":"The only other causal tokenizer that was compared to Cosmos-Tokenizer1 was the CogVideoX-Tokenizer (CITE) that was used in TesserAct, and Cosmos-Tokenizer1 outperformed it on the peak signal to noise (PSNR) reconstruction quality metric by ~3 points at comparable compression ratios when tested on the DAVIS dataset.\nNVIDIA also performed an ablation of their tokenizer at different compression rates which revealed that their tokenizer decreases in reconstruction quality with higher compression rates (as expected), but notably maintained higher than state of the art performance with up to 8x higher compression."}]
16b:["$","h3",null,{"children":"2.3 Pre-trained World Foundation Models"}]
16c:["$","h4",null,{"children":"Diffusion WFMs"}]
16d:["$","p",null,{"children":["Diffusion-based WFMs utilize ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"continuous latent embeddings"}],".\nThe architecture is a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"transformer-based denoiser"}]," (DiT) modified for controllable generation through 3D patchification."]}]
16e:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Conditioning Strategy"}],": Supports image and video conditioning by concatenating frames along the temporal dimension during denoising."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Performance"}],": Yields the highest visual fidelity and 3D consistency in the Cosmos suite."]}],"\n"]}]
16f:["$","h4",null,{"children":"Autoregressive WFMs"}]
170:["$","p",null,{"children":["AR models formulate world simulation as a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"next-token prediction"}]," task using ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"discrete quantized tokens"}],"."]}]
